Respondents </span></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table></div><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Limitation Act (IX of 1908)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Section 142</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">In a suit for declaration of title and recovery of khash possession, the plaintiffs in addition to proving their title to the suit land must prove that the suit has been filed within 12 years from the alleged date of dispossession. In the case in hand, the plaintiffs miserably failed to prove that the suit has been filed within 12 years from the alleged date of dispossession.                        … (23)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Ahmed Miaji and others Vs. Eakub Ali Munshi and others (1960) 12 DLR 708; Syed Moin Ahmed Vs. Khondkar Mohiuddin (1967) 19 DLR and Amanatullah and others Vs. Ali Mohammad Bhuiyan and another, (1997) 2 BLC (AD) 134 ref.</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">For the Appellants: </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">Mr. Mahbubey Alam,</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;"> Attorney General, instructed <span style="letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">by Mr. Haridas Paul, Advocate</span>-on-Record.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">For the Respondents:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">Mr. A. M. Aminuddin, Senior Advocate, <span style="letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">instructed by Mr. Syed Mahbubur</span> Rahman, Advocate-on-Record.</span></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 24.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-variant: small-caps;">Syed Mahmud Hossain, J</span></u></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">: </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">This appeal by leave is directed against the judgment and order dated 08.06.2011 passed by a Single Bench of the High Court Division in Civil Revision No.3070 of 2010 discharging the Rule and affirming the judgment and decree dated 05.04.2010 passed by the learned Additional District Judge, Sixth Court, Dhaka in Title Appeal No.07 of 2009 allowing the appeal and  reversing the judgment and decree dated 28.06.2007 passed by the learned Joint District Judge, Additional Court, Dhaka in Title Suit No.234 of 2003 dismissing the same. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">2.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">The facts, leading to the filing of this appeal, in brief, are :</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">         Al-haj Md. Serajuddin as the plaintiff filed Title Suit No.(number not stated) of 1998 renumbered as Title Suit No.234 of 2003 in the Additional Court of Joint District Judge, Dhaka praying for declaration of title and recovery of khash possession on removing the construction standing on the suit property. His case, in short, is that he purchased the land of ‘Ka’ schedule to the plaint with two storied building, garage, different plants situated on S.A. Dag No.10 of Mouza-Kakrail under previous Lalbagh Police Station now Ramna within Dhaka Collectorate from Syed Farooq Mirja, son of Syed Fakrul Hasan Mirja in 1971. After purchase, the plaintiff got his name mutated and had been paying taxes regularly. While the plaintiff was abroad, the ‘Ka’ schedule was wrongly declared abandoned property. Having come to know of the aforesaid fact, the plaintiff filed an application to the Government of Bangladesh and the Government having been satisfied released the suit property in favour of the plaintiff and issued memo dated 19.06.1983 from the office of defendant No.3 but defendant No.1 did not return the land shown in schedule ‘Kha’ to the plaint. Consequently, the plaintiff filed Title Suit No.53 of 1988 in the Court of Assistant Judge, Fourth Court, Dhaka, which was decreed on 17.12.1988. After that, the plaintiff requested defendant Nos.1 and 2 to deliver ‘Kha’ schedule land to him on a number of dates from 26.03.1989 up to 03.05.1997 and lastly, on 08.07.1997 but defendant No.1 did not vacate or deliver ‘Kha’ schedule land to the plaintiff. As such the plaintiff issued legal notice upon defendant No.1 on 01.09.1997. But defendant No.1 did not pay any heed to the said request made by the plaintiff and consequently, the suit was filed. Along with plaint, the plaintiff filed sketch map showing position of the garage. During pendency of the suit, the sole-plaintiff died and his heirs were substituted as the plaintiffs.        </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%;">3.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%;">Defendant Nos.1 and 3 by filing written statements denying all the material statements made in the plaint. It appears that at first defendant No.3 filed written statement on 30.03.2000 and subsequently on 02.05.2000. In the first written statement, it has been written by defendant No.3 that the suit land was allotted to defendant No.1, vide memo No.2FV-123/72/2103 dated 09.12.1974 at a rental of Tk.1,000/- per month and later on, vide memo No.Sef-V/1M/D7/70 (PT)/402 dated 03.08.1984 to the Ministry of Home Affairs for using the same for the police department. Since then police department had been enjoying the suit schedule-B land. It is further stated that Title Suit No.53 of 1988 was decreed against defendant No.3 on contest and <em>ex parte</em> against defendant Nos.1 and 2. The aforesaid suit was filed by a person who had no right, title, interest and possession in the suit land. Summons of the aforesaid suit was not served upon defendant Nos.1 and 2. The garage mentioned in the instant suit is unspecified and as such, Civil Court Commissioner is required to be appointed to identify the location of the garage. It is further stated that defendant No.1 has been possessing  the property for more than 20 years and as such acquired title by adverse possession. In the second written statement, the Government stated that the suit land had been vested in the Government as per provision of P.O. (President’s Order) No.16 of 1972 as abandoned property by gazette notification No.9762(8) at serial No.10 according to the provision of Ordinance LIV of 1985 on 23.09.1986 and it was allotted to defendant Nos.1 and 2 and they have been possessing the suit schedule-B property. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">4.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The trial Court upon hearing the parties by its judgment and order dated 28.06.2007 dismissed the suit.    </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">5.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Against the judgment and decree passed by the trial Court, the plaintiffs preferred Title Appeal No.07 of 2009 before the learned District Judge, Dhaka. On transfer, the appeal was heard and disposed of by the then learned Additional District Judge, Sixth Court, Dhaka, who by his judgment and order dated 05.04.2010 allowed the appeal reversing the judgment and decree of the trial Court.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">6.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the judgment and decree passed by the appellate Court, the defendants filed a revisional application before the High Court Division and obtained Rule in Civil Revision No.3070 of 2010. The learned Single Judge of the High Court Division by the judgment and order dated 08.06.2011 discharged the Rule with direction affirming the judgment and decree of the appellate Court. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">7.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Feeling aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the judgment and order passed by the High Court Division, the defendant-leave-petitioners have filed Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No.1887 2011 before this Division, in which, leave was granted on 15.09.2014 resulting in Civil Appeal No.230 of 2014. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">8.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Mahbubey Alam, learned Attorney General, appearing on behalf of the leave appellants, submits that the plaintiffs in the plaint alleged that they had been dispossessed in 1974 and Title Suit No.(number not stated) of 1998 renumbered as Title Suit No.234 of 2003 having been filed on 19.02.1998 beyond the statutory period of limitation for recovery of possession, the plaintiffs are not entitled to a decree for recovery of possession in the instant suit. He also submits that the plaintiffs filed Title Suit No. 52 of 1988 for permanent injunction against the appellants and that decree was passed restraining the appellants from changing the nature and character of the suit land and that the plaintiff of that suit had not asserted his possession in the suit land (‘Kha’ schedule land to the plaint) and as such, the decree passed in Title Suit No.52 of 1988 is of no avail to the plaintiffs and even that suit for permanent injunction was also filed beyond the statutory period of limitation of 12 years from his dispossession in 1974. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">9.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Mr. A. M. Aminuddin, learned Senior Advocate, appearing on behalf of the respondents, on the other hand, submits that the suit has been filed within the statutory period of limitation and as such, the High Court Division was justified in discharging the Rule. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">10.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">We have considered the submission of the learned Attorney General for the appellants and the learned Senior Advocate for the respondents, perused the impugned judgment and the materials on record. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">11.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Before entering into the merit of the appeal, it would be pertinent to quote the grounds, for which, leave was granted as under: </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">“The land purchased by the plaintiffs from S.A. Plot No.10 having been recorded in R.S. Plot No.932, the Court of appeal below failed to take into consideration that the garage claimed by the plaintiffs is not within their R.S. Plot No.932; rather the same is within R.S. Plot No.933 which is an abandoned property and under the occupation of Police Department and the High Court Division committed an error in upholding the decision of the Court of appeal below. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">The subject matter of the instant suit being a garage and whether the same is within the purchased land of the plaintiffs or beyond their purchased land being the subject matter of local investigation with reference to their title deeds and in the instant case the plaintiff having not taken any initiative for local investigation, the Court of appeal below illegally decreed the suit and the High Court Division committed error of law in upholding the said decree.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">The plaintiff alleged that they have been dispossessed in the year 1974 and they having filed an earlier suit being Title Suit No.52 of 1988 and in the said suit they having not prayed for recovery of possession from the defendant, the plaintiff is not entitled to a decree for recovery of possession in the instant suit in respect of which they have allegedly been dispossessed in the year 1974.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">12.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">It transpired from the plaint that the original plaintiff, Al-haj Md. Serajuddin purchased the suit land under Holding No.10, New Baily Road in 1971. After the death of the original plaintiff his heirs were substituted in his place as the plaintiffs. They claimed that the suit land is part and parcel of Holding No.10, New Baily Road and not Holding No.10/A, New Baily Road. The plaintiffs alleged that the defendants dispossessed them from the suit land treating it as an abandoned property. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">13.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Admittedly, the plaintiffs filed Title Suit No.53 of 1988 for permanent injunction against (1). Superintendent of Police, Special Branch, 10/A, New Baily Road, Police Station-Ramna, Dhaka, (2) Deputy Inspector General, Special Branch, 10/A, New Baily Road, Police Station-Ramna, Dhaka and (3). Government of Bangladesh, represented by the Secretary, Ministry of Public Works. The plaint of Title Suit No.53 of 1988 was not exhibited. From judgment delivered in Title Suit No.53 of 1988, we find that the learned Assistant Judge, Fourth Court, Dhaka, while describing the case of the plaintiff stated, amongst others, as under:</span> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">“</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: AdarshaLipiExp; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">h¡wm¡­cn plL¡­ll f§aÑ j¿»Z¡m­u 10-H ®hCm£ ®l¡X Y¡L¡ ¢p¢V ®Øfn¡m hË¡’ Y¡L¡ ®L hl¡Ÿ L­lez aMe h¡c£l Ae¤f¤¢ÙÛ­a 1/2<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>ew ¢hh¡c£NZ h¡c£l üaÄ cMm£u Aœ BlS£l ‘M</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: AdarshaLipiExp;">’</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: AdarshaLipiExp; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"> ag¢pm i§J² NÉ¡­lS¢V cMm L­l ®euz</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      <span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">  </span></span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">From the aforesaid averment of the plaint, it appears that even in 1978 the sole plaintiff Al-haj Serajuddin was out of possession of the suit land prior to filing of Title Suit No.53 of 1988 for permanent injunction.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">15.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">From the judgment of Title Suit No.53 of 1988, we find that the Government of Bangladesh, represented by the Secretary, Ministry of Public Works by filing written statement asserted that the disputed ’Kha’ schedule land is part and parcel of Holding No.10/A, of New Baily Road. Defendant No.3 further asserted that defendant Nos.1 and 2 had been in possession of the suit land (‘Kha’ schedule land). Having gone through the judgment delivered in Title Suit No.53 of 1988, we find that the learned Assistant Judge, Fourth Court, Dhaka, restrained the defendants of Title Suit No.53 of 1988 from changing the nature and character of ‘Kha’ schedule land to the plaint by a decree of permanent injunction. From the judgment, it appears that the plaintiff himself admitted that he was out of possession of ‘Kha’ schedule land when the suit for permanent injunction was filed. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">16.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Subsequently, the plaintiff filed present Title Suit No.234 of 2003. The High Court Division having considered the documentary evidence came to a finding that the plaintiff acquired title from the original owner of the suit property who was a non-Bengali. The High Court Division also found that the defendants had no title to the suit land and that they were restrained by an order of permanent injunction for making construction or renovation in the suit land. The High Court Division also found that defendant Nos.1 and 2 had been possessing the suit land on the strength of their possession in the garage defying the decree of the Court passed in Title Suit No.53 of 1988. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">17.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">We have already noticed that even in the plaint of Title Suit No.53 of 1988 for permanent injunction, the  plaintiff Al-haj Md. Serajuddin, the predecessor-in-interest of the plaintiff-respondents of Title Suit No.234 of 2003, stated that he was out of possession of the ‘Kha’ schedule land. Subsequently, the present suit was filed for declaration of title and recovery of possession. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">18.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">P.W.1, Md. Sharifuddin, in his evidence stated that within their boundary the Special Branch had been in possession. He further stated that they (defendants) took possession in <span style="letter-spacing: -0.4pt;">1974 and that subsequently his father filed the suit.</span></span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">19.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Having gone through the record, the judgment delivered in Title Suit No.53 of 1988 and the evidence of P.W.1 given in Title Suit No.234 of 2003, we find that the plaintiff had been out of possession of the suit land (‘Kha’ schedule land) according to their admission from 1974. The present suit for declaration of title and recovery of khash possession was filed in 1998. Therefore, the suit is hopelessly barred by limitation. The plaintiff was required to file the suit for declaration of title and recovery of possession within 12 years from the alleged date of dispossession but they have been failed to do so and as such, they are not entitled to get a decree for recovery of possession. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">20.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of <strong><em>Ahmed Miaji and others vs. Eakub Ali Munshi and others (1960)12 DLR 708</em></strong> it has been held that where the plaintiffs have set up a case of possession followed by dispossession, they must prove possession within 12 years of the suit as contemplated under Article 142 of the Limitation Act.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">21.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of <strong><em>Syed Moin Ahmed vs. Khondkar Mohiuddin (1967) 19 DLR 912</em></strong>, it has been held that under Article 142  of the limitation Act, it is the duty of the plaintiff first to prove to the satisfaction of the Court that he was in possession of the suit premises within 12 years prior to the filing of the suit and if he <span style="letter-spacing: -0.4pt;">fails to do so he cannot get decree for declaration</span> of title and recovery of possession.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">22.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Reliance may be placed on the case of <strong><em>Amanatullah and others vs. Ali Mohammad Bhuiyan and another (1997)2 BLC (AD)134</em></strong> where it has been held as under: </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">“The last but not the least point that has been noticed by this Court at the time of hearing of the appeal is that there is no averment in the plaint of plaintiffs’ dispossession from the suit land within twelve years of bringing the suit which is for recovery of khas possession. Notwithstanding this, both the trial Court <span style="letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">and the lower appellate Court concurrently</span> found that the plaintiffs had never been in possession of the suit land. In such circumstances, the suit was not maintainable. On this ground alone the plaintiffs’ suit was liable for dismissal.” </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">23.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">On consideration of the cases referred to above, it appears that in a suit for declaration of title and recovery of khash possession, the plaintiffs in addition to proving their title to the suit land must prove that the suit has been filed within 12 years from the alleged date of dispossession. In the case in hand, the plaintiffs miserably failed to prove that the suit has been filed within 12 years from the alleged date of dispossession. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">24.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the light of the findings, we are of the view that the High Court Division erroneously decreed the suit for declaration of title and recovery of khash possession. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">         Accordingly, this appeal is allowed and the impugned judgment delivered by the High Court Division is set aside.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><a href="#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" title=""><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11pt;">CIVIL APPEAL No.</span></u></strong></a><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11pt;"> 230 of 2014.</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><span style="font-size: 9pt;">(From the judgment and order dated 08.06.2011 passed by </span><span style="font-size: 9pt; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">the High Court Division in Civil Revision No. 3070 of 2010).</span></span></p></div></div></div></div>

Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="67" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 1 Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="68" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 2 Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="69" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 3 Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="70" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Dark List Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="71" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful Shading Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="72" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful List Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="73" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful Grid Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="60" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light Shading Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="61" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light List Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="62" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light Grid Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="63" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Shading 1 Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="64" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Shading 2 Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="65" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium List 1 Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="66" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium List 2 Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="67" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 1 Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="68" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 2 Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="69" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 3 Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="70" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Dark List Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="71" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful Shading Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="72" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful List Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="73" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful Grid Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="60" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light Shading Accent 6"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="61" Petitioners</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Andadul Huq alias Emdadul Huq and others </span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">...Opposite parties</span></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table></div><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Order 1 Rule 10(2)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 115%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">The learned Joint District Judge failed  to consider the plaintiffs No. 10-15 are the legal heirs of Daimuddin, the present petitioners </span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">are also the legal heirs of the said Daimuddin.</span></strong> <strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">The learned Trial Judge has totally </span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">misconceived</span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;"> the whole case and most illegally</span></strong> <strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">rejected the application for addition of parties</span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;"> without considering the facts that the petitioners are <span style="letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">legal heirs of Daimuddin and </span></span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">non consideration </span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">of that vital fact of the learned</span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;"> Judge committed</span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;"> an error of law </span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">resulting in an error in the decision occasioning</span></strong> <strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">failure of </span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">justice.</span></strong> <strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">Consequently, the application</span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;"> for addition</span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;"> of party is hereby allowed.   ...(16, 17 and 21)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Anil Kumar Singh Vs. Shivnath Mishra 3 S.C.C. Page 149;</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Amal Kumar Vs. Mashihur 30 DLR (SC) Page-244 and</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Mahaluxmi Bank Ltd. Vs. Kamakhyalal AIR 1958 Asam Page-56, ref.</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Mr. Abdul Barek Chowdhury with  </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Mr.</span><span style="font-size: 11pt;"> Md.</span><span style="font-size: 11pt;"> Delwar Hossain, Advocates </span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . . For the petitioners</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">No one appears.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . . For the opposite parties</span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;">JUDGMENT</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. A.K.M. Shahidul Huq, J:</span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> Rejection of the  application  filed by the petitioners  for addition of parties has been challenged by the petitioner by invoking the Revisional Jurisdiction of this Hon’ble Court  as laid down in  Section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure in which  a Division Bench of this Hon’ble Court on perusal of the impugned order dated 9.1.2014 of the learned Joint District Judge, 3rd Court, Dhaka passed in Title Suit No. 343 of 2013 rejecting the application filed by the petitioner for addition of parties the Revisional Application  filed under  Section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure  and on hearing the submissions of the learned Advocate for the petitioner  was pleased to issue  a rule calling upon the opposite parties to show cause as to why  the order dated 09.01.2014 passed by the learned Joint District Judge, 3rd Court, Dhaka in  Title Suit No. 343 of 2013 rejecting the application filed by the petitioner for addition of parties as co-plaintiffs shall not be set aside and/ or such other or further order or orders as to this court may seem fit and proper.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%;">2.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%;">The short facts for disposal of the rule is that to disposal of the rule is that the  opposite party Nos. 1-15 as plaintiffs filed Title Suit No. 260 of 2013 in the 1st court of the Joint District Judge, Dhaka against the opposite party No. 16 for declaration to the effect that they are in 16 annas owners of  the ‘Ka’ schedule  property and that S.A., R.S. and City Jarip Khatians are wrong and not  binding upon the plaintiff. The short facts for disposal of the rule is that the suit land belonged to Ala Baksh by way of C.S. recorded tenant and purchased  said Ala Baksh died leaving four sons and four daughters and wife. The heirs of Ala Baksh made settlement </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%; letter-spacing: -0.2pt;">amongst themselves and four daughters namely-</span> <span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%; letter-spacing: -0.2pt;">Azor Bibi, Salatunnessa, Sahitunnessa, Amirunnessa,</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%;"> wife Saburan Bibi got plot Nos. 2771, are .3150 acres, 2776 acres, .0150 acres, plot No. 2764, an area of .0150 acres and  2767, are .08 acres in total 0.4250 acres and they transferred the same on 16.11.1947 in favour of Daimuddin Mozammal Huq, Emdadul Huq, Sirajul Huq, Nurul Huq. Subsequently Abeda Khatun and Rizia  Khatun as plaintiff filed Title Suit No. 3554 on 20.05.1954 in the 1st Court of Joint Distruct Judge, Dhaka and the said suit was transferred to the 5th Court of Joint District Judge, Dhaka and renumbered as Title Suit No. 04 of 1957 and in that suit the present plaintiff No. 1 was the defendant No. 40, the predecessor of the plaintiff Nos. 2-6 Sirajul Huq was the defendant No. 38, the predecessor of the plaintiff Nos. 7-9 Nurul Huq was the defendant No. 39, the predecessor of the plaintiff Nos. 10-16, Daimuddin was the defendant No. 36. The said suit was decreed on compromise on 13.05.1958 and final decree was drawn on 30.05.1967. In the said Solenama, the defendant Nos. 36-40 got a compact saham on the b asis of the deed dated 16.11.1947 being deed No. 6131. Thereafter, Mozammal Huq died leaving four brothers namely- Daimuddin, Emdadul Huq, Sirajul HJuq and Nurul Huq. Thereafter, Sirajul Huq died leaving the plaintiff Nos. 2-6. Nurul Huq died leaving the plaintiff Nos. 7-9. Daimuddin died leaving the plaintiff Nos. 10-16 and thus the plaintiff became the owner of the suit property and they have been in peaceful possession of the suit property. The defendant claimed the suit property on July 2012 and came to learn that the suit property has been wrongly recorded in the name of the defendant along with others in the S.A. R.S. and City Jarip Khatian and as such the plaintiffs have been compelled to file the present suit for declaration against the defendant.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">3.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the suit stating inter alia that Daimuddin died leaving the plaintiff Nos. 10-15 along with one daughter   namely- Rahija Begum and said Rahija Begum while had been owning and possessing her share in the suit property died leaving the petitioners as her legal heirs and successors and they have been in possession along with the plaintiff and as such the petitioners are necessary parties in the suit.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">4.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The application for addition of party was ultimately heard on 9.01.2014 and the learned Joint District Judge, 3rd Court, Dhaka has been pleased to reject the application for addition of party on misconception of law.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">5.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -0.2pt;">Mr. Abdul Barek Chowdhury, the learned</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> Advocate appearing for the petitioners  submits that  the plaintiff Nos. 10-15 are the legal heirs of late Daimuddin. The present petitioners are also the heirs of late Daimuddin and as such they are necessary party to be added as co-plaintiffs, but the learned Trial Court totally misconceived the whole case and illegally rejected the application for addition of party without considering the fact that the petitioners are the legal heirs of Daimuddin and as such committed an error of law resulting in the decision occasioning failure of justice.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">6.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the petitioners further submits that the relief prayed for by the plaintiff Nos. 10-16 and the relief of the petitioners are same and there is no clash between them and the petitioners as legal heirs of Daimuddin are necessary party and there is no denial that the petitioners are not the legal heirs of Daimuddin and as such the reason that has been shown by the learned Joint District Judge is not cogent and as such committed an error of law resulting in the decision occasioning failure of justice.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">7.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">He also submits that unless the petitioners</span><span style="font-size: 11pt;"> are made party in the suit as co-plaintiff, the multiplicity of suit and litigation will arise and as such the order dated 09.01.2014 passed by the learned Joint District Judge, 3rd Court, Dhaka is under misconception of law resulting in the decision occasioning failure of justice.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">8.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">The learned Advocate for the petitioners next submits that the plaintiff Nos. 10-15 are the legal heirs of late Daimuddin. The present petitioners are also the heirs of late Daimuddin as such they are necessary party to be added as co-plaintiffs, but the learned Trial Court totally misconceived the whole case and illegally rejected the application for addition of party without considering the fact that the petitioners are the legal heirs of Daimuddin and as such committed an error of law resulting in the decision occasioning failure of justice.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">9.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the petitioners also submits that  the relief prayed for by the plaintiff Nos. 10-16 and the relief of the petitioners are same and there is no clash between  them and the petitioners as legal heirs of Daimuddin are necessary party and there is no denial t6hat the petitioners are not the legal heirs of Daimuddin and as such the reason that has been shown by the learned Joint District Judge is not cogent and as such committed an error  of law resulting in the decision  occasioning failure of justice.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">10.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the petitioners lastly submits that  unless the petitioners are  made party in the suit as co-plaintiff, the multiplicity of suit and litigation will arise and as such the order dated 9.01.2014 passed by the learned Joint District Judge, 3rd Court, Dhaka is under misconception of law resulting in the decision occasioning failure of justice.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">11.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">We have heard the learned Advocate, perused the impugned order dated 09.01.2014 passed by the learned Joint District Judge, Dhaka in the Title Suit No. 343 of 2013 rejecting the application filed by the petitioners  for addition of parties  as co- plaintiffs ,the Revisional Application  filed under  Section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure also perused the plaint of the Title Suit No. 343 of 2013 of 3rd Court of Joint District Judge Dhaka also  perused the application for addition of parties  as annexed in Revisional Application as Annexure –B, considered the submissions of the learned Advocate appearing for the petitioners in support of the Revisional Application filed Under Section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure in order to  arrive at a proper findings, we are very much tempted to refer the relevant provision of law  as contained in  order 1 Rule 10(2) of the Code of Civil Procedure  where it is stated that :</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">         “Where a suit  has been instituted the court may at any stage of the proceeding either upon or without any  application of  either parties and on such terms as may appear to the court to justice order that on  upon terms as may appear to the court order that in the said provision of the law  it is stated that “ the presence of such parties  would be necessary in order to enable the court to effectually and completely adjudicating  upon and settle the question infavour in the suit”.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">12.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">This principal of law has been well settled in the case of the Anil Kumar Singh Vs- Shivnath Mishra  reported in 3 S.C.C. Page149 where it is held that  “ The court may at any stage of the proceedings, either upon or without the application of either party, and on  such terms as may appear to the Court to be just, order that the name of any party improperly joined, whether as plaintiff or defendant , be struck out, and that the name of any person who ought to have been  joined, whether  as plaintiff or defendant, or whose  presence before the court may be necessary in order to enable the court effectually and completely to adjudicate upon and settle all the questions involved in the suit be added”.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">13.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">On perusal of the impugned order  we find  that the impugned order  has been passed in utter violation  of the settled principles of law  as decided in the case of   Amal Kumar Vs. Mashihur   reported in 30 DLR (SC) Page-244  where it is held that :</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">“(Order 4, Rule 10(2) of the Code of Civil Procedure empowers the Court to add parties  at any stage of the proceedings, either upon or without application who ought to have  been joined, whether as plaintiff or defendant, or whose presence before the court may be necessary in order to enable the court effectually and completely to adjudicate upon and settle all the questions involved  in the  suit. This power is discretionary. Unless this power is exercised arbitrarily or fancifully it cannot be interfered with under section 115 of the Code of Civil Procedure. Even an improper or wrong exercise of disceretion is not open to revision unless the order is contrary to legal principles governing the exercise of such discretion, or the court has acted perversely”. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">14.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">We find in the case of  Mahaluxmi Bank Ltd. Vs. Kamakhyalal  reported in  AIR 1958 Asam Page-56 where it is held that-</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 109%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.35pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%;">“The every first issue relates to the  question whether the plaintiff is competent to sue. An objection was taken during the pendency of the suit that the person entitled to sue was one S.K. Dutta, who had the authority  to realize  the dues of the bank. This fact was also admitted by the Manager of the Bank, Ranendra Narayan Purkayastha (P.W.1). The plaintiff was, therefore, called upon to produce in Court the scheme  approved by the High Court of Judicature all bank. From this scheme it is clear that the Sylhet Industrial Bank Ltd. Was amalgamated with the plaintiff  bank on 27.06.1947, and under the terms thereof, the whole of the undertaking  assets, properties and liabilities of the transferor company, the Sylhet Industrial  Bank Ltd, were transferred to and did vest in the said transferee company, the plaintiff Mahaluxmi Bank Ltd. The plaintiff bank was further held entitled to continue legal proceedings instituted  by or against the said transferor company. The transferee company was also authorized  to carry on the business of the transferor company at its existing branches and had also the authority to close down such of the branches of the transferor company, as it considered necessary. The Court sanctioned this scheme  under section 153 of the  Indian Companies Act, by an order dated the 1st  April, 1950. It further ordered that Mr. S.K. Dutta, an Advocate of the Court who was a share-holder of the Sylhet Industrial  Bank Ltd. Prior to its amalgamation, should be in charge of the assets of the said Bank and the books of account relating thereto and realization and disbursement of the said assets </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">according to the scheme of amalgamation</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%;"> sanctioned by the Court on the 25th day of June, 1947. It is, therefore,  contended that the plaintiff was not competent to sue any longer. This contention found favour with the learned Sub-ordinate Judge, who held that it was necessary to make Mr. S.K. Dutta, a party to the suit, in view of the objection to defect of party taken in the course of arguments, the plaintiff, on the 4th of September, 1952, filed an application praying that, if necessary, Mr. dutta may be added as a party to the suit, but the Court refused to accept to the prayer, on the ground that the petition had been filed late. This was not an adequate justification to refuse the prayer, if the court considered that the presence of Mr. Dutta was necessary for a proper adjudication of the suit. There was no question of institution involved </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">so as to affect the defendants prejudicially.</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%;"> It is well established that subject to just equities, a party may be added at any stage of the proceedings.”</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">15.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">In view of the above, it is well established</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> that the subject to just equating a party may be added at any stage of the proceedings.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">16.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">We have heard the learned  Advocate appearing for the petitioners  while no one appears on behalf of the opposite parties and perused the impugned order dated 09.01.2014 passed in Title Suit No. 343 of 2013 by the learned Joint District Judge, 3rd Court Dhaka rejecting the application for addition parties, we find the learned Joint District Judge failed  to consider the plaintiffs No. 10-15 are the legal hears of  Daimuddin the present petitioner  are also the legal heirs of the said Daimuddin.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">17.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Trial Judge we find has totally misconceived  the whole case and most illegally rejected the application for addition of parties  without considering the facts that the petitioners are legal heirs of  Daimuddin  and non consideration that vital fact of the learned Judge committed an error of law  resulting in an error in the decision occasioning failure of justice. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">18.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the aforesaid facts and circumstances and the reasons as stated herein before we are of the view that the learned Joint District Judge passed the impugned order based on surmise and conjecture and suffers from serious legal perversity material irregularity and illegality and as such the impugned judgment and order passed by the learned 3<sup>rd</sup> Joint District Judge, Dhaka is not sustainable  under the  provision of  law as contain in Order 1 Rule 10(2) of the Code of Civil Procedure.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">19.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In that view of the matter the impugned judgment and order dated 9.1.2014 passed in Title Suit No. 343 of 2013 rejecting the application for addition of parties is not sustainable in law and the same is liable to be set aside.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">20.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the result the rule is made Absolute without any order as to cost.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">21.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Consequently the application for addition of party is hereby allowed.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">22.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The order of stay all further proceedings of Title Suit No. 343 of 2013 now pending in the court of learned Joint District Judge, 3rd Court,  Dhaka  is hereby recalled and vacated.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">23.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Joint District Judge 3rd Court Dhaka is hereby directed to dispose of  Title suit No. 343 of 2013 expeditiously as far as practicable preferably within four months from the date of receipt of a copy of this judgment positively.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">         The office is hereby directed to transmit a copy of this judgment to the concern court forthwith for information and necessary action.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><a href="#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" title=""><span style="font-size: 10pt; letter-spacing: -0.2pt;">Civil Revision No. 1869 of 2014.</span></a></span></p></div></div></div></div>
495	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Jamuna Resort Ltd. Vs. Bangladesh Bridge Authority 2017 (1) LNJ 226</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Revision No. 984 of 2015 </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  A. K. M. Shahidul Huq.. J.</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Rafique-ul-Huq, Mr. Abdun Nur,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2017 (1) LNJ 226</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2016</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Jamuna Resort Ltd.</p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Bangladesh Bridge Authority</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Civil Law</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2017-04-12</p><!DOCTYPE html><p><!-- [if gte mso 9]><xml>
