The commitment of the respondent No.1 to inspect fire and safety facilities of readymade garments factories in Bangladesh at their own expenses is no doubt a welcome step for the improvement and development of the infrastructure of garments factories in the country. In the process they are assisting the Inspector General of Factories of the Government in ensuring fire and building safety of readymade garments factories in the country. Respondent No.1 has accordingly inspected over 1500 garments factories in the country and found some of them to be non compliant and lacking adequate facilities on fire and building safety. Thus it is apparent that the respondent No.1 has been acting with the consent of the Inspector General of factories and assisting it in inspecting and ensuring the safety of the garments factories in the country and therefore performing functions” in connection with the affairs of the Republic”. </span></span></p><p class="CM7" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">40.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Furthermore the Respondent No 1 has been performing a public function and acting in the public domain.The facts seem to be similar to the aforesaid Datafin case. Thus the petitioner’s application under Article 102(1) is maintainable on this ground as well. </span></span></p><p class="CM5" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">41.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the instant case the petitioner’s right to profession trade and business as guaranteed by Article 40 of the Constitution has been infringed by the arbitrary act of the Respondent No.1 in publishing/showing the name of the petitioner as a non compliant and unsafe garments factory in its website without inspecting it and therefore in the opinion of this Court the Rule is not only maintainable under Article 102(1 but has substance. </span></span></p><p class="CM5" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">42.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">For Article 102 (2) to be attracted however the petitioner must be aggrieved by an action of a person performing functions “in connection with the affairs of the Republic”, or local authority or statutory body and he should be without any other alternative remedy or redress . The remedy sought by the petitioner is simply a direction on the Respondent No.1 for inspecting the petitioner’s factory and publishing the findings in its website. If the petitioner’s factory is unsafe and not fit in any way then the Respondent No.1 has nothing to loose. The petitioner cannot seek remedy from the Civil Court or any other forum in the form of a direction since there is no contractual relationship with the respondent No.1. Similarly an action for defamation also will not serve any purpose since the petitioner wants the Respondent No.1 to publish the accurate condition of its factory. Thus to compel the Respondent No. 1 to inspect its factory and publish the findings in its website the petitioner does not appear to have any other alternative remedy. In such view of the matter therefore this Rule is also maintainable under Article 102(2). </span></span></p><p class="CM5" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">43.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the instant case it is admitted that the <span style="letter-spacing: -0.4pt;">respondent No.1 never inspected the petitioner's</span> factory but relied upon a report submitted by the respondent No.3 who inspected the petitioner's factory at the request of the respondent No.2 on 18.5.2013 after Accord was created although Clause 10 of the Accord Agreement clearly stipulates that all garments factories would be inspected by an independent internationally reputed Inspector appointed by Accord. The petitioner's factory was never inspected by an Inspector appointed by the Respondent No.1 despite several requests by the petitioner and the Government. The respondent no. 1 without inspecting the petitioner’s factory published its name in its website and stated it to be a non compliant and unsafe factory resulting in adverse publicity of the petitioner's garments factory causing all European buyers not only to cancel their existing orders but also refrain from giving future orders to the petitioner factory. Due to the adverse report of the respondent No.1 in its website even American buyers of readymade garments represented by Alliance refrained from giving orders to the petitioner causing it huge financial and economic loss and driving it to bankruptcy. </span></span></p><p class="CM5" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">44.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The contention of the respondents that the petitioner’s factory was not inspected by the Respondent No. 1 as it did not comply with its report to make certain structural improvements of its factory building is misconceived since there is no such precondition for inspecting a factory in the Accord Agreement and therefore the arbitrary insistence of such condition prior to inspecting the petitioner's factory is illegal and not sustainable in law. Furthermore, in the inspection report of the respondent No.3 although certain apprehensions have been expressed regarding safety of the petitioner's factory, no specific and detailed corrective measures was suggested and therefore the petitioner was justified in requesting the inspection of his factory by the respondent No.1 or its appointed Safety Inspector to specify the nature of correctional works required for the petitioner's factory so that compliance may be made to the satisfaction of the said respondent. The arbitrary imposition of pre-conditions by the respondent No.1 for inspecting the petitioner's factory and publishing a report containing adverse remarks in its website has caused serious damage and loss to the petitioner which could have been easily avoided by the respondent No.1 by merely inspecting it as it did in the case of other garments factories. This policy of pick and choose, of inspecting some factories and not inspecting the petitioner's factory cannot be condoned or approved by any standard of fairness. The Respondent No.1 Accord was acting in concert with the Inspector General of Factories of the Government of Bangladesh through the National Tripartite Action Committee to ensure the safety of ready made garments factories in Bangladesh and therefore the Respondent No.1 was acting in connection with the affairs of the Republic . Their failure to act in accordance with law, by publishing a report in their website about the petitioner’s factory without inspecting it is a breach of Clause 10 of their own agreement and the action may be subject to judicial review under Article 102(2) of the Constitution also. </span></span></p><p class="CM5" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 105%;">45.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 105%;">The submission by the learned Advocate for the respondent No.1 that if a direction is given to the respondent No.1 to inspect the petitioner's factory it will open up the floodgates for other non compliant factories to come to this Court and obtain similar orders is misconceived since it has not been denied that the petitioner is the only factory whose name has been published on the respondent No.1’s website as a non compliant factory without inspecting it. Had the petitioner's factory been inspected it could seek relief before the Review Panel. Other non compliant factories therefore have every opportunity to review the decision by the Review panel. </span></span></p><p class="CM21" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">46.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">It is not for this court to decide whether the petitioner's factory is safe for manufacturing garments or direct any particular foreign buyer to place orders with the petitioner. The foreign buyers are free to decide where to place their orders and from which source to procure their products; what this court is concerned about is that the petitioner’s name should not be published in the website of the Respondent No.1 as a non compliant/ unsafe factory without any prior inspection in accordance with the terms and conditions enumerated in its own Agreement. </span></span></p><p class="CM21" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">47.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">It is to be noted that the respondent No.4 (National Tripartite Committee headed by the Secretary, Ministry of Labour and Employment) as well as the respondent No.5 (Inspector General of Factories of the Government of Bangladesh ) requested the respondent No.1 to inspect the petitioner's factory but the request was not complied with and since the respondents did not have any binding contractual relationship with the respondent No.1 they were unable to compel it to comply with their request. The petitioner therefore had no other choice but to approach this court and invoke the special jurisdiction under Article 102 of the Constitution. </span></span></p><p class="CM21" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">48.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The petitioner’s application is thus not only maintainable both under Article 102(1) as well as under Article 102(2) and also has substance for the reasons stated above. </span></span></p><p class="CM21" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">49.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Accordingly, the Rule is made absolute. </span></span></p><p class="CM5" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">50.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The respondent No.1 is directed to immediately arrange for inspection of the petitioner's factory as per Clause 10 of the Accord Agreement and other necessary protocols and publish the inspection report in its website and circulate it among its members all over the world. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">         There will be no order as to costs.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.35pt; mso-pagination: none; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; punctuation-wrap: simple; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Ed. </span></strong></span></p><p class="Default"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"> </span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><a href="#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" title=""><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 110%;">Writ Petition No. 10929 of 2015</span></strong></a></span></p></div></div></div></div>
497	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Md. Monirul Islam Vs. The State 2017 (1) LNJ 197</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 45447 of 2013 With Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 45448 of 2013 </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  A. K. M. Shahidul Huq. J.</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. A.B.M. Waliur Rahman, Mr. Nazmul Karim Khan,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2017 (1) LNJ 197</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2016</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Md. Monirul Islam </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  The State </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Criminal Law</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2017-04-11</p><!DOCTYPE html><p><!-- [if gte mso 9]><xml> <w:WordDocument> <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="64" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Shading 2 Accent 2"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="65" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium List 1 Accent 2"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="66" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium List 2 Accent 2"/>  <w:LsdException Name="Medium Grid 2 Accent 2"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="69" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 3 Accent 2"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="70" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Dark List Accent 2"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="71" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful Shading Accent 2"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="72" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful List Accent 2"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="73" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful Grid Accent 2"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="60" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light Shading Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="61" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light List Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="62" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Petitioner</span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 9pt;">(In both cases)</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Evidence Act (I of 1872)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Section 114(f)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">General Clauses Act (X of 1897)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Section 27</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The implication of illustration (f) of section 114 of the Evidence Act and the provision of section 27 of General Clauses Act are that in case of posting of letter, sending notice or summons by registered post to the correct address or to the address of the addressee known to the sender i.e. while no other address of the addressee was made known to the sender or, in other words, change of address of the addressee was not intimated to the sender, the presumption is that such letter, notice or summons sent by registered post to the person addressed to have been delivered and if the registered envelope  is returned with the endorsement of the postal peon “refused” by the addressee, then too it shall be considered that the letter, notice and the summons has duly and properly been received or served unless the addressee establishes that letter, notice or summons was not sent to his correct address and as such, he had no occasion to refuse the acceptance of the registered letter or the envelop. The person who is disputing or trying to deny the statutory presumption of the matter as provided by the provision of section 27 of the General Clauses Act and that the presumption of correctness or genuineness of the matter as implied by illustration (f) of section 114 of the Evidence Act is to rebut the said matter or genuineness/correctness of presumption of fact upon producing evidence. So, letter sent, notice or summons sent by registered post and if returned with the endorsement “refused” shall be accepted as good and due service of notice or summons and the delivery of the letter to the person addressed unless the addressee rebuts the presumption of good service or delivery of letter by adducing evidence. . . . (39)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 10.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Quader Chowdhury and others Vs. The State, 28 DLR (AD) 38; Eusof Babu Vs. The State 68, DLR (AD) 298; Sheikh Mashuk Rahman Vs. The State and another, 62 DLR 2010 28; Md. Kamal Uddin @ Md. Kamal Ahmed Vs. Md. Mezbah Uddin and another, XI ADC 2014; Abdul Alim Vs. Biswajit Dey and another, 59 DLR (2007) 236; Abdur Rob Molla Vs. Shahabuddin Ahmed and others, 12 BLC (AD) 2007, 188; AIR PC 102; 52 CWN 659; 39 CWN 934; 6 DLR 267; 17 DLR (WP) 26; 22 DLR 664; Sarwar Hossain Moni (Md) Vs. The State and another, 66 DLR (AD) 2014 283; Abdur Rob Molla Vs. Shahabuddin Ahmed and others, 12 BLC (AD) 2007, 118; Harihar Banerji and others Vs. Ramshashi Roy and others, AIR 1981 PC 102; Monomohan Roy Chowdhury Vs. Ajit Kamal Dutta, 6 DLR 267; Dr. Jamshed Bakht Vs. Md. Kamaluddin, 1981 BLD 97; of Sheikh Mashuk Rahman Vs. The State and another, 62 DLR 2010, 28 and M.K. Bazlur Rahman Vs. Md. Johurul Haque and another, VI ADC (2009) 809 ref.</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; letter-spacing: -0.3pt; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Mr. A.B.M. Waliur Rahman Khan, with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Mr. Khairul Alam, Advocates.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">… For the Petitioner</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Mr. Nazmul Karim, Advocate </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . . For the opposite party No. 2.    </span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;">JUDGMENT</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.35pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">A. K. M. Shahidul Huq, J:</span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> The facts and law involved in the above noted two Criminal Miscellaneous Cases are being identical, as such, both the rules are taken up together for analogous hearing and disposal by this common judgment.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">2.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -0.2pt;">The proceedings of Metropolitan Sessions</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> Case No. 207 of 2012 arising out of C.R. Case No. 321 of 2011 under section 138 of the Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881 (as amended in 2006) now pending in the Court of learned Joint Metropolitan Sessions Judge, 7<sup>th</sup> Court Dhaka has been called in question by invoking the inherent jurisdiction of the criminal proceedings as laid down in section 561-A of the Code of Criminal Procedure in which a Division Bench of this Hon’ble Court was  pleased to issue a rule </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">calling upon the opposite party to show cause as to why the proceedings of Metropolitan Sessions Case No. 207 of 2012 arising out of C.R. Case No. 32 of 2011 under section 138 of the Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881 as amended on 2006 now pending in the Court of Joint Metropolitan Sessions Judge, 7<sup>th</sup> Court Dhaka should not be quashed and/or pass such other or further order or orders as to this Court may seem fit and proper.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">3.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">The short facts leading to the disposal of the case is that one Nawab Auto Rice and Feed Mills (Pvt.) Limited, Room No. 6, G/7 (1<sup>st</sup> floor), Bazar Road, Block-F, Mohammadpur, Dhaka 1207 as complainant filed a petition of complaint being petition Case No. 321 of 2012 before the Court of learned Chief Metropolitan Magistrate, Dhaka.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">4.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Under Section 138 of the Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881 (as amended in 2006) alleging inter alia that the complainant is a rice processing company and the accused is a businessmen by profession who carrying on his business under the name and style of his proprietorship concern namely M/S. Monir Enterprise. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">5.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In course of business the accused has issued a Cheque No. IBB 4546833 dated 23.06.2011 for an amount of Tk. 51,00,000,00 in favour of the complainant drawn on the Current Account being No. 01016532 under the name and style of his aforesaid proprietorship concern, maintained with the Islami Bank Bangladesh Limited, Chapainawabgonj Branch, Chapainawabgonj.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">6.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The complainant presented the aforesaid cheque for collection through his account and <span style="letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">the same has been dishonored due to insufficient</span> found vide Memo dated 10.08.2011 issued by the Islami Bank Bangladesh Limited, Chapai-nawabgonj Branch, Chapainawabgonj. Despite repeated persuasion and all dispute cooperation <span style="letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">by the above cheque amount to the complainant.</span> </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">7.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In compliance with section 138 of the Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881 (as amended) the complainant served legal notice on 21.08.2011.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">8.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In that notice the complainant requested the accused to pay the cheque amount of Tk. 51,00,000/- within 30 (thirty) days from the date of receipt of the notice along with a note that in the event of default to pay the cheque <span style="letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">amount proceedings under Negotiable Instrument</span> Act shall be lodged against the accused. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">9.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The complainant further alleged that the said notice was returned showing the remark </span></span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: ArhialkhanMJ;">ÔcÖvcK †gvevBj gva¨‡g wPwV MÖnb Kwi‡Z A¯^xKvi Kivq g‡Z †dirÕ</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"> on 08.09.2011.</span> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      <span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">  </span></span></span></span></strong><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">It is stated that the accused-petitioner was</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> <span style="letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">enlarged on bail by the court below and thereafter</span> the case transferred to the Court of learned Joint Metropolitan Sessions Judge, 7<sup>th</sup> Court, Dhaka for holding trial and Registered as Metropolitan Sessions Case No. 207 of 2012. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">11.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">It is stated that on 11.08.2013 the date was fixed for framing of charge against the accused-petitioner and the accused-petitioner duly appeared before the court and the learned Judge-in-charge of Joint Metropolitan Sessions Judge, 7<sup>th</sup> Court, Dhaka was pleased to fix the next date of the case on 07.10.2013 for order. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">12.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">It is stated that the accused-petitioner filed an application under section 265C of the Code of Criminal Procedure before the Court of learned Joint Metropolitan Sessions Judge, 7<sup>th</sup> Court, Dhaka for discharging him from the case and the same is pending for hearing. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">13.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The accused-petitioner is a poor man and the accused-petitioner and the complainant <span style="letter-spacing: -0.4pt;">used to run his business by the accused-petitioner</span> as benamder and he made the business institution in the name of the accused-petitioner by financing him and also made account in the name of the accused-petitioner by his money but while the accused-petitioner refused to carry on the business of the complainant as benamder he filed the instant case against the accused-petitioner with ulterior motive and malafide intention and as such the impugned order is liable to be quashed for ends of justice.   </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">14.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. A.B.M. Waliur Rahman Khan, the learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the petitioner submits that the mandatory provision of section 138 of the Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881 has not been complied with because the complainant did not serve legal notice upon the accused petitioner but in the petition of complaint the complainant falsely alleged that the accused did not receive the same and as such the impugned proceeding against the accused petitioner is liable to be quashed for ends of justice.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">15.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate next submits that the accused petitioner did not give any cheque to the complainant because the cheque book was kept at the office o the complainant as the accused-petitioner carried on business of the accused petitioner but while the accused-petitioner left the office of the complainant he used the said cheque against the accused-petitioner and as such the impugned proceeding against the accused petitioner is liable to be quashed for ends of justice.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">16.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate or the petitioner further submits that the Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881 is a special law and provision of this Act to be construed strictly light variation giving a different meaning of the intent of the legislature is not punishable and as such the proceeding of this case is to be quashed for ends of justice. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">17.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the petitioner by filing supplementary affidavit tries to submits that according to section 141 (b) of the Negotiable Instruments Act the cause of action to file the complaint is arisen within thirty days from the receipt of the notice as per clause (c) of the section 138(1) of the Act and in the instant complaint petition it is found legal notice was served on 23.08.2011 which was returned on 08.09.2011 being refused by the accused-petitioner over mobile and as such the cause of action will be counted from 08.09.2011 having knowledge about the notice and if within 08.10.2011 no payment is found to have been paid cause of action would be arisen but in the instant case cognizance is found to have been taken on 26.09.2011 which is before the expiry of the stipulated period as laid down under section 138(1)(c) of the Act for which reason the instant proceeding can not be allowed to be proceeded in the eye of law. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">18.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the petitioner tries to draw our attention to the effect that in order to initiate a case under section 138 of the Negotiable Instrument Act according to section 1(A) of the said section the notice required to be served under clause (b) of sub section (1) shall be served in the following manner:-</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(a)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">    </span></span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">by delivering it to the person on whom it is to be served;</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">(b)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">   </span></span><span style="font-size: 11pt;">by sending it by registered post with acknowledgement due to that person at his usual or lost known place of abode or business in Bangladesh. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(c)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">    </span></span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">by publication in a Daily Bangla National Newspaper having wide circulation. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new
